<process_isolation>
CRITICAL: Multiple pipeline runs may execute simultaneously on this machine. `ps aux | grep method.py` matches ALL runs, not just yours.
- NEVER kill processes by name (`killall`, `pkill -f`, `ps aux | grep ... | xargs kill`). This kills OTHER runs' processes.
- NEVER monitor processes by name (`ps aux | grep method.py`). You will see other runs' processes and get confused.
- ALWAYS use PID-based process management:
  Run: `uv run method.py & PID=$!` or `timeout <seconds> uv run method.py & PID=$!`
  Check: `kill -0 $PID 2>/dev/null && echo "Running" || echo "Ended"`
  Stop: `kill $PID`
  Wait: `wait $PID; echo "Exit code: $?"`
  Monitor: `tail -f logs/run.log & TAIL_PID=$!` then `kill $TAIL_PID` when done
</process_isolation>

### [3] SYSTEM-USER prompt · 2026-07-09 00:47:13 UTC

````
<hypothesis>
kind: hypothesis
title: Percolation Threshold Readability Model
hypothesis: >-
  Text readability correlates with the percolation threshold of a cohesion network constructed from the text. As a reader
  processes a text, they build a mental network where sentences are nodes and cohesion links (lexical overlap, semantic similarity,
  referential ties) are edges. The ease of comprehension correlates with how quickly the mental network percolates (forms
  a giant component). The percolation threshold of the text's cohesion network serves as a measurable proxy for this cognitive
  integration difficulty. Preliminary experiments using TF-IDF similarity and lexical overlap on synthetic texts show a positive
  correlation (r=0.724, p<0.001) between percolation threshold and grade level, explaining 52.5% of variance as a single feature.
  However, this relationship requires validation on real-world educational text datasets and with semantic embeddings (SBERT)
  rather than TF-IDF alone. The percolation threshold captures complementary information to traditional surface-level readability
  metrics, as a combined model (percolation + traditional metrics) achieves R²=0.921, suggesting the threshold measures a
  distinct aspect of readability related to discourse cohesion and cognitive integration rather than surface features alone.
motivation: >-
  Current readability formulas (Flesch-Kincaid, BERT-based models) measure surface features or use black-box predictions,
  but they don't model the underlying cognitive process of how readers integrate information. Percolation theory from statistical
  physics provides a natural model: reading comprehension is the process of building a connected mental model. The percolation
  threshold precisely captures how easily this model integrates. This gives a physically interpretable readability metric
  grounded in how the brain actually processes cohesive text.
assumptions:
- >-
  Reader comprehension involves building a connected mental network of concepts from the text
- >-
  Cohesion links (lexical overlap, semantic similarity, reference) correspond to edges in the reader's mental network
- >-
  The ease of comprehension correlates with how quickly the mental network percolates (forms a giant component)
- >-
  The percolation threshold of the text's cohesion network is a measurable proxy for this cognitive integration difficulty
investigation_approach: >-
  1. Construct cohesion networks from English texts: nodes = sentences, edges = cosine similarity of sentence embeddings (SBERT)
  + lexical overlap. 2. Compute percolation threshold by simulating edge addition in random order and measuring when giant
  component emerges (reaches 50% of nodes). 3. Compare percolation threshold against gold-standard readability scores (Flesch-Kincaid,
  human ratings from Newsela/OneStopEnglish datasets). 4. Test whether percolation threshold predicts reading comprehension
  scores better than traditional formulas. 5. Ablate: test with/without semantic edges to isolate effect of cohesion vs. just
  lexical overlap.
success_criteria: >-
  1. Percolation threshold should correlate negatively with established readability scores (easy texts have low thresholds).
  2. Percolation threshold should explain variance in human readability ratings beyond traditional formulas (significant delta
  R²). 3. On sentence-level readability datasets (Weebit, Newsela), percolation threshold should achieve RMSE < 1.5 grade
  levels when used as a feature in a simple linear model. 4. The method should be robust: threshold should be similar across
  multiple random edge-ordering runs (std < 0.05).
related_works:
- >-
  Zhang et al. (2026) 'Automatic text readability assessment for educational content based on graph representation learning'
  (Scientific Reports) - Uses Graph Convolutional Networks on POS-based dependency graphs. Our approach differs fundamentally:
  we use percolation theory to model the DYNAMIC process of comprehension (when does the mental model connect?) rather than
  static graph classification. GCNs learn to predict readability from graph structure; we derive an interpretable physical
  parameter (percolation threshold) that directly models cognitive integration.
- >-
  Ehret (2018) 'Kolmogorov complexity as a universal measure of language complexity' - Uses compression-based complexity.
  Our approach differs: we model TEXT AS A NETWORK and measure connectivity emergence, not information density. Kolmogorov
  complexity captures overall difficulty; percolation threshold captures specifically how fragmented vs. integrated the text
  feels.
- >-
  Cohen et al. on semantic network percolation (creativity research) - Uses k-clique percolation to measure flexibility of
  free association networks. Our work adapts percolation theory to a completely different domain (readability assessment)
  with a different network construction (text cohesion vs. free association) and a different research question (predicting
  readability vs. measuring creativity).
inspiration: >-
  Percolation theory from statistical physics (studying phase transitions in networks) crossed with discourse cohesion theory
  from linguistics. In physics, percolation threshold predicts when a material becomes conductive; in reading, we hypothesize
  it predicts when a text becomes 'comprehensible' (when the reader's mental model forms a connected whole). The key cross-domain
  insight: readability is not a static property of text but emerges from a phase transition in the reader's mental network.
terms:
- term: Percolation threshold
  definition: >-
    In network science, the critical fraction of edges that must be present before a giant connected component emerges spanning
    a significant portion of the network
- term: Cohesion network
  definition: >-
    A graph representation of text where nodes represent sentences or concepts, and edges represent cohesive ties such as
    lexical overlap, semantic similarity, or referential connections
- term: Giant connected component
  definition: >-
    A subgraph that contains a large fraction of all nodes in the network and in which any two nodes are connected by a path
- term: Phase transition
  definition: >-
    In statistical physics, a point at which a system undergoes a qualitative change in behavior (e.g., from disconnected
    to connected) as a parameter crosses a critical threshold
- term: SBERT
  definition: >-
    Sentence-BERT: a modification of BERT that uses siamese/triplet networks to produce semantically meaningful sentence embeddings
    for measuring similarity
summary: >-
  We propose that text readability equals the percolation threshold of the text's cohesion network. Easy texts have low thresholds
  (concepts connect quickly into a coherent mental model); hard texts have high thresholds (concepts remain fragmented). This
  provides a physically interpretable readability metric based on network science.
_relation_rationale: >-
  Narrowed scope to match actual evidence; reduced claim strength from 'equals' to 'correlates with'
_confidence_delta: decreased
_key_changes:
- >-
  Changed 'readability equals' to 'readability correlates with' based on limited evidence (correlation not causation)
- >-
  Added explicit acknowledgment that current evidence is limited to synthetic texts with TF-IDF (not SBERT as originally claimed)
- >-
  Added requirement for real-world validation on educational datasets (OneStopEnglish, CommonLit, CEFR-SP)
- >-
  Added note about complementary information beyond traditional metrics based on combined model R²=0.921
- >-
  Reduced scope from definitive claim to proof-of-concept requiring further validation
- >-
  Updated investigation approach to reflect actual experiment: TF-IDF similarity (not SBERT), 240 synthetic texts (not 12,469
  real texts)
relation_type: evolution
</hypothesis>

  performance (R², RMSE), ablation results, and disaggregated results by dataset
approach: >-
  1. DATASET: Load the three datasets from art_AXDjT-jFuQog (OneStopEnglish: 567 texts, CommonLit: 4,724, CEFR-SP: 7,178 =
  12,469 total). 2. SBERT IMPLEMENTATION: Use sentence-transformers all-MiniLM-L6-v2 to compute sentence embeddings. Construct
  cohesion networks with: (a) Semantic edges: cosine similarity > 0.5, (b) Lexical edges: POS-filtered content word overlap
  > 0.3. 3. PERCOLATION: Compute threshold via random edge ordering (N=50 iterations, α=0.5 Giant component threshold). 4.
  EVALUATION: Compute Pearson r, Spearman ρ, R², RMSE against grade levels. Disaggregate by dataset. 5. ABLATION: Run semantic-only
  and lexical-only variants. 6. COMMONLIT CIRCULARITY: Compute correlation between percolation threshold and Flesch-Kincaid
  directly; report OneStopEnglish results separately as independent validation. 7. OUTPUT: Generate full_method_out.json with
  all results, following the schema with predict_percolation field for each example.

Let me start by:
1. Understanding the dataset structure from the dependency
2. Researching SBERT and percolation threshold computation
3. Creating a detailed plan

Actually, looking at the instructions more carefully, I see that I should output the plan as JSON to a specific file. Let me structure my response properly.

Key elements I need to include:


1. Title - short and jargon-free
2. Summary - brief overview
3. runpod_compute_profile - based on the computational needs (SBERT embeddings for 12,469 texts suggests GPU might be helpful)
4. implementation_pseudocode - detailed pseudocode
5. fallback_plan - what to do if primary approach fails
6. testing_plan - how to validate

I need to be specific about:
- How to load the data from the dependency
- How to implement SBERT embeddings
- How to construct cohesion networks
- How to compute percolation thresholds
- How to evaluate
- Output format

Let me think about the compute profile. SBERT embeddings for 12,469 texts - each text has multiple sentences. This could be computationally intensive. 

The CommonLit dataset's 4,724 literary excerpts suggest substantial text processing requirements. I'll need a GPU profile to handle the embedding generation efficiently. The computational complexity of generating sentence-level embeddings across multiple datasets demands significant parallel processing capabilities.

Careful resource allocation will be critical to manage the embedding generation and network construction within reasonable time constraints. I'll explore the percolation threshold computation and SBERT embedding approach, focusing on the experimental design and computational strategy. The method involves constructing a semantic network using sentence-level embeddings, with a nuanced approach to edge generation and component analysis.

The computational workflow requires careful consideration of embedding techniques and network construction parameters. Specifically, the approach needs robust methods for generating sentence representations and defining meaningful connectivity thresholds.

Preliminary investigation suggests potential challenges in scaling the network analysis across diverse text collections, particularly with varying document lengths and complexity. I'll continue the percolation threshold calculation, focusing on the component size tracking and threshold determination:

        track component sizes using union-find
        monitor largest component's growth
        when largest component reaches 50% of nodes, record edge fraction as threshold
        repeat process 50 times with randomized edge orderings
        compute mean and standard deviation of threshold values

The approach explores network connectivity by systematically adding edges and observing component formation dynamics. I'll track the largest component's growth, calculating the percolation threshold when it reaches 50% of nodes. By averaging results across 50 random edge orderings, I'll determine the mean threshold and standard deviation. This approach allows robust measurement of network connectivity emergence.

The method systematically explores how network components evolve, providing insights into the critical point of large-scale connectivity. I'll track the percolation threshold calculation, focusing on the key steps of edge addition and component size monitoring. The process involves systematically adding edges and tracking the largest component's growth to determine the critical connectivity point.

As edges are added randomly, I'll monitor the largest component's size relative to the total network. When this component reaches 50% of total nodes, I'll record the fraction of edges added as the percolation threshold. This approach provides insight into the network's connectivity emergence.

The method requires multiple iterations with randomized edge orderings to ensure robust threshold estimation, capturing the probabilistic nature of network formation. I'll continue the pseudocode for the ablation and evaluation process, focusing on the key steps of comparing different edge types and assessing their predictive performance:

        # Explore semantic and lexical edge contributions
        for edge_type in ['semantic', 'lexical']:
            percolation_values = compute_percolation(edge_type)
            evaluate_predictive_power(percolation_values, grade_levels)
        
        # Assess model performance across datasets
        for dataset in ['OneStopEnglish', 'CommonLit', 'CEFR-SP']:
            performance_metrics = calculate_metrics(percolation_values, grade_levels)
            visualize_results(dataset, performance_metrics)
        
        # Investigate potential correlations with traditional readability metrics
        correlation_analysis(percolation_values, flesch_kincaid_scores)

The approach systematically examines how different edge types and datasets impact the percolation-based readability prediction, providing a comprehensive evaluation strategy. I'll continue the thought about the CommonLit dataset concern and the need for independent validation:

Explore potential circularity in the CommonLit dataset by carefully examining the grade level assignments. Lexical Overlap\n- POS-filtered content word overlap > 0.3\n- Need NLTK or spaCy for POS tagging\n\n### 4. Dataset Loading\n- Load from dependency artifact (art_AXDjT-jFuQog)\n- Three datasets: OneStopEnglish, CommonLit, CEFR-SP\n- Total: 12,469 texts\n\n### 5. Evaluation Metrics\n- Pearson correlation r\n- Spearman \u03c1\n- R\u00b2 (variance explained)\n- RMSE (grade level prediction error)\n\n### 6. Computational Considerations\n- 12,469 texts - need efficient implementation\n- SBERT embedding computation - can be parallelized\n- Network percolation - O(E) per iteration, run 50 iterations\n- Use CPU parallelism (multiprocessing) for batch processing\n\n## Plan Structure\n1. ### [27] TOOL CALL — file_editor · 2026-07-09 00:50:02 UTC

```
{
  "command": "create",
  "path": "/ai-inventor/aii_data/runs/run_LOb33NvVGQcB/3_invention_loop/iter_2/gen_plan/gen_plan_experiment_1/.sdk_openhands_agent_struct_out.json",
  "file_text": "{\n  \"title\": \"Test percolation readability on 12k texts\",\n  \"summary\": \"Implement percolation threshold readability model using SBERT embeddings on 12,469 real-world texts from three datasets (OneStopEnglish, CommonLit, CEFR-SP). Compute correlations with grade level, evaluate predictive performance (R\u00b2, RMSE), run ablation studies, and report disaggregated results by dataset.\",\n  \"runpod_compute_profile\": \"cpu_heavy\",\n  \"implementation_pseudocode\": \"# STEP 1: Load dependency dataset\\nimport json\\nimport sys\\nsys.path.append('/ai-inventor/aii_data/runs/run_LOb33NvVGQcB/3_invention_loop/iter_1/gen_art/gen_art_dataset_1')\\nfrom data import load_dataset\\n\\n# Load all three datasets\\ndatasets = ['onestopenglish', 'commonlit', 'cefrsp']\\nall_texts = []\\nfor dataset_name in datasets:\\n    data = load_dataset(dataset_name)  # Returns list of {input: text, output: grade_level}\\n    for item in data:\\n        item['dataset'] = dataset_name\\n        all_texts.append(item)\\n# Total: 12,469 texts\\n\\n# STEP 2: SBERT Embedding Computation\\nfrom sentence_transformers import SentenceTransformer\\nimport numpy as np\\nfrom multiprocessing import Pool, cpu_count\\n\\nmodel = SentenceTransformer('all-MiniLM-L6-v2')\\n\\ndef get_sentence_embeddings(text):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Split text into sentences and compute SBERT embeddings\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    sentences = text.split('. ')  # Simple sentence splitting\\n    if len(sentences) < 2:\\n        return None, None  # Skip single-sentence texts\\n    embeddings = model.encode(sentences)\\n    return sentences, embeddings\\n\\n# Parallel processing for efficiency\\nwith Pool(cpu_count()) as pool:\\n    results = pool.map(get_sentence_embeddings, [t['input'] for t in all_texts])\\n\\n# STEP 3: Cohesion Network Construction\\nimport networkx as nx\\n\\ndef compute_cosine_similarity(emb1, emb2):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Cosine similarity between two embeddings\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    return np.dot(emb1, emb2) / (np.linalg.norm(emb1) * np.linalg.norm(emb2) + 1e-8)\\n\\ndef get_content_words(sentence):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Extract content words (nouns, verbs, adjectives, adverbs) using POS tagging\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    import nltk\\n    from nltk import pos_tag, word_tokenize\\n    try:\\n        tokens = word_tokenize(sentence.lower())\\n        tagged = pos_tag(tokens)\\n        content_pos = {'NN', 'VB', 'JJ', 'RB', 'NNS', 'VBP', 'JJR', 'JJS'}\\n        return set([t[0] for t in tagged if any(t[1].startswith(pos) for pos in content_pos)])\\n    except:\\n        return set()\\n\\ndef lexical_overlap(sent1, sent2):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute lexical overlap ratio of content words\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    words1 = get_content_words(sent1)\\n    words2 = get_content_words(sent2)\\n    if not words1 or not words2:\\n        return 0.0\\n    overlap = len(words1.intersection(words2))\\n    return overlap / max(len(words1), len(words2))\\n\\ndef build_cohesion_network(sentences, embeddings):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Build cohesion network with semantic and lexical edges\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    n = len(sentences)\\n    G = nx.Graph()\\n    G.add_nodes_from(range(n))\\n    \\n    edges = []\\n    for i in range(n):\\n        for j in range(i+1, n):\\n            # Semantic edge: cosine similarity > 0.5\\n            sim = compute_cosine_similarity(embeddings[i], embeddings[j])\\n            semantic_edge = sim > 0.5\\n            \\n            # Lexical edge: content word overlap > 0.3\\n            lex_sim = lexical_overlap(sentences[i], sentences[j])\\n            lexical_edge = lex_sim > 0.3\\n            \\n            if semantic_edge or lexical_edge:\\n                edges.append((i, j, {'semantic': sim, 'lexical': lex_sim}))\\n    \\n    G.add_edges_from(edges)\\n    return G, edges\\n\\n# STEP 4: Percolation Threshold Computation\\ndef compute_percolation_threshold(G, edges, n_iterations=50, alpha=0.5):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute percolation threshold via random edge ordering\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    n_nodes = G.number_of_nodes()\\n    target_size = int(alpha * n_nodes)\\n    thresholds = []\\n    \\n    for _ in range(n_iterations):\\n        # Random edge ordering\\n        shuffled_edges = edges.copy()\\n        np.random.shuffle(shuffled_edges)\\n        \\n        # Add edges incrementally and track giant component\\n        temp_G = nx.Graph()\\n        temp_G.add_nodes_from(range(n_nodes))\\n        \\n        for idx, (u, v, _) in enumerate(shuffled_edges):\\n            temp_G.add_edge(u, v)\\n            # Check largest connected component\\n            components = list(nx.connected_components(temp_G))\\n            largest = max(len(c) for c in components)\\n            \\n            if largest >= target_size:\\n                threshold = idx / len(shuffled_edges)\\n                thresholds.append(threshold)\\n                break\\n        else:\\n            thresholds.append(1.0)  # Never reached threshold\\n    \\n    return np.mean(thresholds), np.std(thresholds)\\n\\n# STEP 5: Main Processing Loop\\nresults = []\\nfor idx, (text_item, (sentences, embeddings)) in enumerate(zip(all_texts, results)):\\n    if sentences is None:\\n        continue  # Skip single-sentence texts\\n    \\n    # Build network\\n    G, edges = build_cohesion_network(sentences, embeddings)\\n    \\n    # Compute percolation threshold\\n    mean_threshold, std_threshold = compute_percolation_threshold(G, edges)\\n    \\n    # Store results\\n    results.append({\\n        'id': idx,\\n        'dataset': text_item['dataset'],\\n        'text': text_item['input'][:200] + '...',  # Truncate for output\\n        'grade_level': text_item['output'],\\n        'percolation_threshold': mean_threshold,\\n        'percolation_std': std_threshold,\\n        'n_sentences': len(sentences),\\n        'n_edges': len(edges)\\n    })\\n    \\n    if idx % 100 == 0:\\n        print(f'Processed {idx}/{len(all_texts)} texts')\\n\\n# STEP 6: Evaluation\\nimport scipy.stats as stats\\n\\n# Convert to arrays\\npercolation_vals = np.array([r['percolation_threshold'] for r in results])\\ngrade_vals = np.array([r['grade_level'] for r in results])\\n\\n# Pearson correlation\\npearson_r, pearson_p = stats.pearsonr(percolation_vals, grade_vals)\\n\\n# Spearman correlation\\nspearman_r, spearman_p = stats.spearmanr(percolation_vals, grade_vals)\\n\\n# R\u00b2 (variance explained)\\nfrom sklearn.linear_model import LinearRegression\\nmodel = LinearRegression()\\nmodel.fit(percolation_vals.reshape(-1, 1), grade_vals)\\nr2 = model.score(percolation_vals.reshape(-1, 1), grade_vals)\\n\\n# RMSE\\nfrom sklearn.metrics import mean_squared_error\\npredictions = model.predict(percolation_vals.reshape(-1, 1))\\nrmse = np.sqrt(mean_squared_error(grade_vals, predictions))\\n\\n# STEP 7: Disaggregated Results by Dataset\\nfor dataset_name in datasets:\\n    subset = [r for r in results if r['dataset'] == dataset_name]\\n    if not subset:\\n        continue\\n    subset_perc = np.array([r['percolation_threshold'] for r in subset])\\n    subset_grade = np.array([r['grade_level'] for r in subset])\\n    \\n    r, p = stats.pearsonr(subset_perc, subset_grade)\\n    print(f'{dataset_name}: r={r:.3f}, p={p:.4f}, n={len(subset)}')\\n\\n# STEP 8: Ablation Studies\\n# Run with semantic-only edges (no lexical)\\n# Run with lexical-only edges (no semantic)\\n# Compare correlations\\n\\n# STEP 9: Output Results\\noutput = {\\n    'method': 'percolation_threshold_readability',\\n    'total_texts': len(results),\\n    'overall_metrics': {\\n        'pearson_r': pearson_r,\\n        'pearson_p': pearson_p,\\n        'spearman_r': spearman_r,\\n        'spearman_p': spearman_p,\\n        'r2': r2,\\n        'rmse': rmse\\n    },\\n    'disaggregated': {},\\n    'predict_percolation': results  # One entry per text\\n}\\n\\nwith open('full_method_out.json', 'w') as f:\\n    json.dump(output, f, indent=2)\\n\\nprint('Experiment complete. Results saved to full_method_out.json')\",\n  \"fallback_plan\": \"If primary approach fails:\\n\\n1. SBERT memory issues: Use smaller model (paraphrase-MiniLM-L3-v2) or batch processing with smaller batch sizes\\n\\n2. NetworkX too slow for large networks: \\n   - Implement percolation using adjacency matrix operations with NumPy\\n   - Skip texts with >100 sentences (likely noise)\\n   - Use approximate percolation (check every 10 edges instead of every edge)\\n\\n3. Percolation computation too slow:\\n   - Reduce iterations from 50 to 10\\n   - Implement early stopping when giant component reaches threshold\\n   - Use Union-Find data structure for faster component tracking\\n\\n4. Dataset loading fails:\\n   - Load JSON files directly from full_data_out.json\\n   - Parse expected format: {input: text, output: grade_level}\\n\\n5. NLTK/POS tagging fails:\\n   - Use simple lexical overlap (all words, not just content words)\\n   - Use TF-IDF vectorization as fallback for semantic similarity\\n\\n6. general performance issues:\\n   - Process only 10% sample (1,247 texts) for proof of concept\\n   - Use only OneStopEnglish dataset (567 texts) if others fail\\n   - Skip ablation studies if time runs out\\n\\n7. Output validation fails:\\n   - Ensure predict_percolation field has all required fields\\n   - Validate against schema before saving\\n   - Save partial results if full processing fails\",\n  \"testing_plan\": \"Testing strategy (gradual scaling):\\n\\n1. UNIT TESTS (before full run):\\n   - Test SBERT embedding on 5 sample sentences\\n   - Test network construction on 3-sample text (5 sentences)\\n   - Test percolation threshold on small network (10 nodes)\\n   - Verify cosine similarity computation\\n   - Verify lexical overlap computation\\n\\n2. MINI DATA TEST (100 texts):\\n   - Run full pipeline on 100 random texts\\n   - Verify output JSON schema matches expected format\\n   - Check that percolation thresholds are in [0, 1] range\\n   - Verify correlations are computed correctly\\n   - Ensure no NaN or infinite values\\n\\n3. SINGLE DATASET TEST (OneStopEnglish, 567 texts):\\n   - Process only OneStopEnglish dataset first\\n   - Verify correlations make sense (should be positive: harder texts have higher thresholds)\\n   - Check that percolation_std < 0.05 for most texts\\n   - Verify RMSE is reasonable (< 2 grade levels)\\n\\n4. ABLATION VALIDATION:\\n   - Run semantic-only variant on 100 texts\\n   - Run lexical-only variant on 100 texts\\n   - Compare correlations to full model\\n   - Verify semantic+lexical > semantic-only \u2248 lexical-only\\n\\n5. SCALING TEST (1,000 texts):\\n   - Process 1,000 texts to verify performance\\n   - Monitor memory usage (should stay < 16GB)\\n   - Estimated time: ~30 minutes for 1k texts\\n   - Extrapolate to 12,469 texts (~6 hours)\\n\\n6. CONFIRMATION SIGNALS (proceed if these hold):\\n   - Pearson r > 0.3 on mini test\\n   - Percolation thresholds vary across texts (std > 0.1)\\n   - No errors in network construction\\n   - Output JSON validates against schema\\n\\n7. ERROR HANDLING TEST:\\n   - Test with malformed text (empty, single sentence, very long)\\n   - Verify graceful handling (skip or default values)\\n   - Check that 95%+ texts process successfully\\n\\nStart with unit tests, then mini test, then scale up. Stop and debug if any test fails.\"\n}\n",

')  # Simple sentence splitting\\n    if len(sentences) < 2:\\n        return None, None  # Skip single-sentence texts\\n    embeddings = model.encode(sentences)\\n    return sentences, (np.linalg.norm(emb1) * np.linalg.norm(emb2) + 1e-8)\\n\\ndef get_content_words(sentence):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Extract content words (nouns, verbs, adjectives, adverbs) using POS tagging\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n words2:\\n        return 0.0\\n    overlap = len(words1.intersection(words2))\\n    return overlap / max(len(words1), len(words2))\\n\\ndef build_cohesion_network(sentences, embeddings):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Build cohesion network with semantic and lexical edges\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    n = len(sentences)\\n    G = nx.Graph()\\n    G.add_nodes_from(range(n))\\n    \\n    edges = []\\n    for i in return G, edges\\n\\n# STEP 4: Percolation Threshold Computation\\ndef compute_percolation_threshold(G, edges, n_iterations=50, alpha=0.5):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute percolation threshold via random edge ordering\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    n_nodes = G.number_of_nodes()\\n    target_size = int(alpha * n_nodes)\\n    thresholds = []\\n    \\n    for _ in range(n_iterations):\\n        # Random edge ordering\\n        shuffled_edges = edges.copy()\\n        np.random.shuffle(shuffled_edges)\\n        \\n        # Add edges incrementally and track giant component\\n        temp_G = nx.Graph()\\n component\\n            components = list(nx.connected_components(temp_G))\\n            largest = max(len(c) for c in components)\\n            \\n            if largest >= target_size:\\n \\n    return np.mean(thresholds), np.std(thresholds)\\n\\n# STEP 5: Main Processing Loop\\nresults = []\\nfor idx, (text_item, (sentences, embeddings)) in enumerate(zip(all_texts, results)):\\n    if sentences is None:\\n        continue  # Skip single-sentence texts\\n    \\n    # Build network\\n    G, edges = build_cohesion_network(sentences, embeddings)\\n    \\n    # Compute percolation    - RMSE < 1.5 grade levels on sentence-level datasets
   - Robustness: std < 0.05 across random runs

1. Add Flesch-Kincaid computation for the CommonLit circularity check

3. Make sure the output format matches the expected schema

Wait, let me re-read the hypothesis:
- "Text readability correlates with the percolation threshold"
- "Preliminary experiments show a positive correlation (r=0.724) between percolation threshold and grade level"
- So higher grade level (harder text) = higher percolation threshold
- That means positive correlation with grade level, which means negative correlation with "readability" if readability is inverted (higher = easier)

Actually, in the success criteria: "Percolation threshold should correlate negatively with established readability scores (easy texts have low thresholds)."


So I need to measure the correlation correctly. Established readability scores like Flesch-Kincaid give higher scores for harder texts (higher grade level), so percolation threshold should correlate POSITIVELY with grade level and with Flesch-Kincaid. correlation\\nspearman_r, spearman_p = stats.spearmanr(percolation_vals, grade_vals)\\n\\n# R\u00b2 (variance explained)\\nfrom sklearn.linear_model import LinearRegression\\nmodel =   "new_str": "# STEP 1: Load dependency dataset and compute traditional readability metrics\nimport json\nimport sys\nimport re\nimport numpy as np\nfrom multiprocessing import Pool, cpu_count\n\nsys.path.append('/ai-inventor/aii_data/runs/run_LOb33NvVGQcB/3_invention_loop/iter_1/gen_art/gen_art_dataset_1')\nfrom data import load_dataset\n\n# Load all three datasets\ndatasets = ['onestopenglish', 'commonlit', 'cefrsp']\nall_texts = []\nfor dataset_name in datasets:\n    data = load_dataset(dataset_name)  # Returns list of {input: text, output: grade_level}\n    for item in data:\n        item['dataset'] = dataset_name\n        all_texts.append(item)\n# Total: 12,469 texts\n\n# Compute Flesch-Kincaid for circularity check and baseline comparison\ndef compute_flesch_kincaid(text):\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute Flesch-Kincaid Grade Level\\\"\\\"\\\"\n    sentences = [s.strip() for s in re.split(r'[.!?]+', text) if s.strip()]\n    words = text.split()\n    \n    if len(sentences) == 0 or len(words) == 0:\n        return 0.0\n    \n    # Count syllables (approximation)\n    def count_syllables(word):\n        word = word.lower()\n        syllables = 0\n        vowels = 'aeiouy'\n        prev_was_vowel = False\n        for char in word:\n            is_vowel = char in vowels\n            if is_vowel and not prev_was_vowel:\n                syllables += 1\n            prev_was_vowel = is_vowel\n        if word.endswith('e'):\n            syllables -= 1\n        if word.endswith('le') and len(word) > 2 and word[-3] not in vowels:\n            syllables += 1\n        if syllables == 0:\n            syllables = 1\n        return syllables\n    \n    total_syllables = sum(count_syllables(w) for w in words)\n    \n    # Flesch-Kincaid Grade Level\n    asl = len(words) / len(sentences)  # Average Sentence Length\n    asw = total_syllables / len(words)  # Average Syllables per Word\n    fk_grade = 0.39 * asl + 11.8 * asw - 15.59\n    \n    return max(0.0, min(12.0, fk_grade))  # Clamp to [0, 12]\n\n# Add Flesch-Kincaid to all texts\nfor item in all_texts:\n    item['flesch_kincaid'] = compute_flesch_kincaid(item['input'])\n\n# STEP 2: SBERT Embedding Computation\nfrom sentence_transformers import SentenceTransformer\n\nprint(\"Loading SBERT model...\")\nmodel = SentenceTransformer('all-MiniLM-L6-v2')\n\ndef get_sentence_embeddings(text):\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Split text into sentences and compute SBERT embeddings\\\"\\\"\\\"\n    sentences = [s.strip() + '.' for s in text.split('.') if s.strip()]\n    if len(sentences) < 2:\n        return None, None  # Skip single-sentence texts\n    embeddings = model.encode(sentences, show_progress_bar=False)\n    return sentences, embeddings\n\n# Parallel processing for efficiency\nprint(f\"Processing {len(all_texts)} texts with SBERT...\")\nwith Pool(cpu_count()) as pool:\n    embedding_results = pool.map(get_sentence_embeddings, [t['input'] for t in all_texts])\n\n# STEP 3: Cohesion Network Construction\nimport networkx as nx\nimport nltk\nfrom nltk import pos_tag, word_tokenize\n\n# Ensure NLTK data is available\ntry:\n    nltk.data.find('tokenizers/punkt')\nexcept LookupError:\n    nltk.download('punkt')\ntry:\n    nltk.data.find('taggers/averaged_perceptron_tagger')\nexcept LookupError:\n    nltk.download('averaged_perceptron_tagger')\n\ndef compute_cosine_similarity(emb1, emb2):\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Cosine similarity between two embeddings\\\"\\\"\\\"\n    return np.dot(emb1, emb2) / (np.linalg.norm(emb1) * np.linalg.norm(emb2) + 1e-8)\n\ndef get_content_words(sentence):\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Extract content words (nouns, verbs, adjectives, adverbs) using POS tagging\\\"\\\"\\\"\n    try:\n        tokens = word_tokenize(sentence.lower())\n        tagged = pos_tag(tokens)\n        content_pos = {'NN', 'VB', 'JJ', 'RB', 'NNS', 'VBP', 'JJR', 'JJS', 'NNP', 'NNPS'}\n        return set([t[0] for t in tagged if any(t[1].startswith(pos) for pos in content_pos)])\n    except:\n        return set()\n\ndef lexical_overlap(sent1, sent2):\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute lexical overlap ratio of content words\\\"\\\"\\\"\n    words1 = get_content_words(sent1)\n    words2 = get_content_words(sent2)\n    if not words1 or not words2:\n        return 0.0\n    overlap = len(words1.intersection(words2))\n    return overlap / max(len(words1), len(words2))\n\ndef build_cohesion_network(sentences, embeddings, use_semantic=True, use_lexical=True):\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Build cohesion network with semantic and/or lexical edges\\\"\\\"\\\"\n    n = len(sentences)\n    G = nx.Graph()\n    G.add_nodes_from(range(n))\n    \n    edges = []\n    for i in range(n):\n        for j in range(i+1, n):\n            semantic_edge = False\n            lexical_edge = False\n            sim = 0.0\n            lex_sim = 0.0\n            \n            if use_semantic:\n                sim = compute_cosine_similarity(embeddings[i], embeddings[j])\n                semantic_edge = sim > 0.5\n            \n            if use_lexical:\n                lex_sim = lexical_overlap(sentences[i], sentences[j])\n                lexical_edge = lex_sim > 0.3\n            \n            if (use_semantic and semantic_edge) or (use_lexical and lexical_edge):\n                edges.append((i, j, {'semantic': sim, 'lexical': lex_sim}))\n    \n    G.add_edges_from(edges)\n    return G, edges\n\n# STEP 4: Percolation Threshold Computation (optimized with Union-Find)\nclass UnionFind:\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Union-Find data structure for efficient component tracking\\\"\\\"\\\"\n    def __init__(self, n):\n        self.parent = list(range(n))\n        self.size = [1] * n\n        self.max_size = 1\n    \n    def find(self, x):\n        while self.parent[x] != x:\n            self.parent[x] = self.parent[self.parent[x]]\n            x = self.parent[x]\n        return x\n    \n    def union(self, x, y):\n        px, py = self.find(x), self.find(y)\n        if px == py:\n            return\n        if self.size[px] < self.size[py]:\n            px, py = py, px\n        self.parent[py] = px\n        self.size[px] += self.size[py]\n        self.max_size = max(self.max_size, self.size[px])\n\ndef compute_percolation_threshold(n_nodes, edges, n_iterations=50, alpha=0.5):\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute percolation threshold via random edge ordering using Union-Find\\\"\\\"\\\"\n    target_size = int(alpha * n_nodes)\n    thresholds = []\n    \n    for _ in range(n_iterations):\n        # Random edge ordering\n        shuffled_indices = np.random.permutation(len(edges))\n        \n        uf = UnionFind(n_nodes)\n        threshold = 1.0  # Default if never reaches threshold\n        \n        for idx in range(len(shuffled_indices)):\n            edge_idx = shuffled_indices[idx]\n            u, v, _ = edges[edge_idx]\n            uf.union(u, v)\n            \n            if uf.max_size >= target_size:\n                threshold = (idx + 1) / len(edges)\n                break\n        \n        thresholds.append(threshold)\n    \n    return np.mean(thresholds), np.std(thresholds)\n\n# STEP 5: Main Processing Loop\nprint(\"Computing percolation thresholds...\")\nresults = []\n\nfor idx, (text_item, emb_result) in enumerate(zip(all_texts, embedding_results)):\n    sentences, embeddings = emb_result\n    if sentences is None:\n        continue  # Skip single-sentence texts\n    \n    # Build network with both semantic and lexical edges\n    G, edges = build_cohesion_network(sentences, embeddings, use_semantic=True, use_lexical=True)\n    \n    if len(edges) == 0:\n        # No edges found, assign threshold = 1.0 (max difficulty)\n        mean_threshold, std_threshold = 1.0, 0.0\n    else:\n        # Compute percolation threshold\n        mean_threshold, std_threshold = compute_percolation_threshold(len(sentences), edges)\n    \n    # Store results\n    results.append({\n        'id': idx,\n        'dataset': text_item['dataset'],\n        'text': text_item['input'][:200] + '...' if len(text_item['input']) > 200 else text_item['input'],\n        'grade_level': text_item['output'],\n        'flesch_kincaid': text_item['flesch_kincaid'],\n        'percolation_threshold': float(mean_threshold),\n        'percolation_std': float(std_threshold),\n        'n_sentences': len(sentences),\n        'n_edges': len(edges)\n    })\n    \n    if (idx + 1) % 100 == 0:\n        print(f'Processed {idx + 1}/{len(all_texts)} texts')\n\nprint(f\"Completed processing {len(results)} texts\")\n\n# STEP 6: Evaluation Metrics\nimport scipy.stats as stats\nfrom sklearn.linear_model import LinearRegression\nfrom sklearn.metrics import mean_squared_error\n\n# Convert to arrays\npercolation_vals = np.array([r['percolation_threshold'] for r in results])\ngrade_vals = np.array([r['grade_level'] for r in results])\nfk_vals = np.array([r['flesch_kincaid'] for r in results])\n\n# Primary correlation: percolation threshold vs grade level (should be POSITIVE)\npearson_r, pearson_p = stats.pearsonr(percolation_vals, grade_vals)\nspearman_r, spearman_p = stats.spearmanr(percolation_vals, grade_vals)\n\nprint(f\"\\\\n=== MAIN RESULTS ===\")\nprint(f\"Percolation vs Grade Level: r={pearson_r:.4f}, p={pearson_p:.6f}\")\n\n# R\u00b2 and RMSE\nlr_model = LinearRegression()\nlr_model.fit(percolation_vals.reshape(-1, 1), grade_vals)\nr2 = lr_model.score(percolation_vals.reshape(-1, 1), grade_vals)\npredictions = lr_model.predict(percolation_vals.reshape(-1, 1))\nrmse = np.sqrt(mean_squared_error(grade_vals, predictions))\n\nprint(f\"R\u00b2 = {r2:.4f}\")\nprint(f\"RMSE = {rmse:.4f} grade levels\")\n\n# Traditional metrics baseline (Flesch-Kincaid)\nfk_pearson_r, fk_pearson_p = stats.pearsonr(fk_vals, grade_vals)\nfk_lr = LinearRegression()\nfk_lr.fit(fk_vals.reshape(-1, 1), grade_vals)\nfk_r2 = fk_lr.score(fk_vals.reshape(-1, 1), grade_vals)\n\nprint(f\"\\\\n=== BASELINE COMPARISON ===\")\nprint(f\"Flesch-Kincaid vs Grade Level: r={fk_pearson_r:.4f}, R\u00b2={fk_r2:.4f}\")\n\n# Combined model (percolation + Flesch-Kincaid)\nfrom sklearn.linear_model import Ridge\nX_combined = np.column_stack([percolation_vals, fk_vals])\ncombined_model = Ridge()\ncombined_model.fit(X_combined, grade_vals)\ncombined_r2 = combined_model.score(X_combined, grade_vals)\nprint(f\"Combined model R\u00b2 = {combined_r2:.4f} (\u0394R\u00b2 = {combined_r2 - max(r2, fk_r2):.4f})\")\n\n# STEP 7: Disaggregated Results by Dataset\nprint(f\"\\\\n=== DISAGGREGATED RESULTS ===\")\ndisaggregated = {}\nfor dataset_name in datasets:\n    subset = [r for r in results if r['dataset'] == dataset_name]\n    if not subset:\n        continue\n    subset_perc = np.array([r['percolation_threshold'] for r in subset])\n    subset_grade = np.array([r['grade_level'] for r in subset])\n    subset_fk = np.array([r['flesch_kincaid'] for r in subset])\n    \n    r_val, p_val = stats.pearsonr(subset_perc, subset_grade)\n    fk_r, fk_p = stats.pearsonr(subset_fk, subset_grade)\n    \n    disaggregated[dataset_name] = {\n        'n': len(subset),\n        'pearson_r': float(r_val),\n        'pearson_p': float(p_val),\n        'flesch_kincaid_r': float(fk_r),\n        'mean_threshold': float(np.mean(subset_perc)),\n        'std_threshold': float(np.std(subset_perc))\n    }\n    \n    print(f\"{dataset_name}: n={len(subset)}, percolation r={r_val:.3f} (p={p_val:.4f}), FK r={fk_r:.3f}\")\n\n# STEP 8: Ablation Studies\nprint(f\"\\\\n=== ABLATION STUDIES ===\")\nablation_results = {}\n\nfor ablation_name, (use_sem, use_lex) in [('semantic_only', (True, False)), ('lexical_only', (False, True)), ('full', (True, True))]:\n    ablation_thresholds = []\n    \n    # Process subset embeddings, use_semantic=use_sem, use_lexical=use_lex)\n        \n        if len(edges) == 0:\n            ablation_thresholds.append(1.0)\n        else:\n            mean_thresh, _ = compute_percolation_threshold(len(sentences), edges, n_iterations=20)\n            ablation_thresholds.append(mean_thresh)\n    \n    subset_grades = [results[i]['grade_level'] for i in subset_indices if embedding_results[i][0] is not None]\n    ablation_thresholds = ablation_thresholds[:len(subset_grades)]\n    \n    if len(ablation_thresholds) > 10:\n        r_val, p_val = commonlit_results])\n    cl_fk = np.array([r['flesch_kincaid'] for r in commonlit_results])\n    circ_r, circ_p = stats.pearsonr(cl_perc, cl_fk)\n    print(f\"CommonLit: Percolation vs Flesch-Kincaid r={circ_r:.3f} (p={circ_p:.4f})\")\n    print(f\"  (High correlation would indicate circularity issue)\")\n\n# STEP 10: Output Results\noutput = {\n    'method': 'percolation_threshold_readability',\n 'combined_r2': float(combined_r2),\n        'delta_r2': float(combined_r2 - max(r2, fk_r2))\n    },\n    'disaggregated': disaggregated,\n    'ablation': ablation_results,\n    'circularity_check': all('percolation_threshold' in r for r in output['predict_percolation'])\nassert all('grade_level' in r for r in output['predict_percolation'])\n\nwith open('full_method_out.json', 'w') as f:\n    json.dump(output, f, indent=2)\n\nprint('\\\\nExperiment complete. all_texts])\n    84\t\n    85\t# STEP 3: Cohesion Network Construction\n    86\timport networkx as nx\n    87\timport nltk\n    88\tfrom nltk import pos_tag, word_tokenize\n    89\t\n    90\t# Ensure NLTK data is available\n    91\ttry:\n    92\t    nltk.data.find('tokenizers/punkt')\n    93\texcept LookupError:\n    94\t    nltk.download('punkt')\n    95\ttry:\n    96\t emb2):\n   101\t    \\\"\\\"\\\"Cosine similarity between two embeddings\\\"\\\"\\\"\n   102\t    return np.dot(emb1, emb2) / (np.linalg.norm(emb1) * np.linalg.norm(emb2) + 1e-8)\n   103\t\n   104\tdef get_content_words(sentence):\n   105\t    \\\"\\\"\\\"Extract content words (nouns, verbs, adjectives, adverbs) using POS tagging\\\"\\\"\\\"\n   106\t    try:\n   107\t        tokens = word_tokenize(sentence.lower())\n   108\t        tagged = pos_tag(tokens)\n   109\t        content_pos = {'NN', 'VB', 'JJ', 'RB', 'NNS', 'VBP', 'JJR', 'JJS', 'NNP', 'NNPS'}\n   110\t        return set([t[0] for t in tagged if any(t[1].startswith(pos) for pos in content_pos)])\n   111\t    except:\n   112\t        return set()\n   113\t\n   114\tdef lexical_overlap(sent1, sent2):\n   115\t    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute lexical overlap ratio of content words\\\"\\\"\\\"\n   116\t    words1 = get_content_words(sent1)\n   117\t    words2 = get_content_words(sent2)\n   118\t    if not words1 or not words2:\n   119\t        return 0.0\n   120\t    overlap = len(words1.intersection(words2))\n   121\t    return overlap / max(len(words1), len(words2))\n   122\t\n   123\tdef build_cohesion_network(sentences, embeddings, use_semantic=True, use_lexical=True):\n   124\t    \\\"\\\"\\\"Build cohesion network with semantic and/or lexical edges\\\"\\\"\\\"\n   125\t    n = len(sentences)\n   126\t    G = nx.Graph()\n   127\t    G.add_nodes_from(range(n))\n   128\t    \n   129\t    edges = []\n   130\t    for i in range(n):\n   131\t        for j in range(i+1, n):\n   132\t            semantic_edge = False\n   133\t            lexical_edge = False\n   134\t            sim = 0.0\n   135\t            lex_sim = 0.0\n   136\t            \n   137\t            if use_semantic:\n   138\t                sim = compute_cosine_similarity(embeddings[i], embeddings[j])\n   139\t                semantic_edge = sim > 0.5\n   140\t            \n   141\t            if use_lexical:\n   142\t                lex_sim = lexical_overlap(sentences[i], sentences[j])\n   143\t                lexical_edge = lex_sim > 0.3\n   144\t            \n   145\t            if (use_semantic and semantic_edge) or (use_lexical and lexical_edge):\n   146\t                edges.append((i, j, {'semantic': sim, 'lexical': lex_sim}))\n   147\t    \n   148\t    G.add_edges_from(edges)\n   149\t    return G, edges\n   150\t\n   151\t# STEP 4: Percolation Threshold Computation (optimized with Union-Find)\n   152\tclass UnionFind:\n   153\t    \\\"\\\"\\\"Union-Find data structure for efficient component tracking\\\"\\\"\\\"\n   154\t    def __init__(self, n):\n   155\t        self.parent = list(range(n))\n   156\t        self.size = [1] * n\n   157\t        self.max_size = 1\n   158\t    \n   159\t    def find(self, x):\n   160\t        while self.parent[x] != x:\n   161\t            self.parent[x] = self.parent[self.parent[x]]\n   162\t            x = self.parent[x]\n   163\t        return x\n   164\t    \n   165\t    def union(self, x, y):\n   166\t        px, py = self.find(x), self.find(y)\n   167\t        if px == py:\n   168\t            return\n   169\t        if self.size[px] < self.size[py]:\n   170\t            px, py = py, px\n   171\t        self.parent[py] = px\n   172\t        self.size[px] += self.size[py]\n   173\t        self.max_size = max(self.max_size, self.size[px])\n   174\t\n   175\tdef compute_percolation_threshold(n_nodes, edges, n_iterations=50, alpha=0.5):\n   176\t    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute percolation threshold via random edge ordering using Union-Find\\\"\\\"\\\"\n   177\t    target_size = int(alpha * n_nodes)\n   178\t    thresholds = []\n   179\t    \n   180\t    for _ in range(n_iterations):\n   181\t        # Random edge ordering\n   182\t        shuffled_indices = np.random.permutation(len(edges))\n   183\t        \n   184\t        uf = UnionFind(n_nodes)\n   185\t        threshold = 1.0  # Default if never reaches threshold\n   186\t        \n   187\t        for idx in range(len(shuffled_indices)):\n   188\t            edge_idx = shuffled_indices[idx]\n   189\t            u, v, _ = edges[edge_idx]\n   190\t            uf.union(u, v)\n   191\t            \n   192\t            if uf.max_size >= target_size:\n   193\t                threshold = (idx + 1) / len(edges)\n   194\t                break\n   195\t        \n   196\t        thresholds.append(threshold)\n   197\t    \n   198\t    return np.mean(thresholds), np.std(thresholds)\n   199\t\n   200\t# STEP 5: Main Processing Loop\n   201\tprint(\"Computing percolation thresholds...\")\n   202\tresults = []\n   203\t\n   204\tfor idx, (text_item, emb_result) in enumerate(zip(all_texts, embedding_results)):\n   205\t    sentences, embeddings = emb_result\n   206\t    if sentences is None:\n   207\t        continue  # Skip single-sentence texts\n   208\t    \n   209\t    # Build network with both semantic and lexical edges\n   210\t    G, edges = build_cohesion_network(sentences, embeddings, use_semantic=True, use_lexical=True)\n   211\t    \n   212\t    if len(edges) == 0:\n   213\t        # No edges found, assign threshold = 1.0 (max difficulty)\n   214\t        mean_threshold, std_threshold = 1.0, 0.0\n   215\t    else:\n   216\t        # Compute percolation threshold\n Compute correlations with grade level, evaluate predictive performance (R\u00b2, RMSE), run ablation studies, and report disaggregated results by dataset.\",\n  \"runpod_compute_profile\": \"cpu_heavy\",\n  \"implementation_pseudocode\": \"# STEP 1: Load dependency dataset\\nimport json\\nimport sys\\nsys.path.append('/ai-inventor/aii_data/runs/run_LOb33NvVGQcB/3_invention_loop/iter_1/gen_art/gen_art_dataset_1')\\nfrom data import load_dataset\\n\\n# Load all three datasets\\ndatasets = ['onestopenglish', 'commonlit', 'cefrsp']\\nall_texts = []\\nfor dataset_name in datasets:\\n    data = load_dataset(dataset_name)  # Returns list of {input: text, output: grade_level}\\n    for item in data:\\n        item['dataset'] = dataset_name\\n        all_texts.append(item)\\n# Total: 12,469 texts\\n\\n# STEP 2: SBERT Embedding Computation\\nfrom sentence_transformers import SentenceTransformer\\nimport numpy as np\\nfrom multiprocessing import Pool, cpu_count\\n\\nmodel = SentenceTransformer('all-MiniLM-L6-v2')\\n\\ndef get_sentence_embeddings(text):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Split text into sentences and compute SBERT embeddings\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    sentences = text.split('. embeddings\\n\\n# Parallel processing for efficiency\\nwith Pool(cpu_count()) as pool:\\n    results = pool.map(get_sentence_embeddings, [t['input'] for t in all_texts])\\n\\n# STEP 3: Cohesion Network Construction\\nimport networkx as nx\\n\\ndef compute_cosine_similarity(emb1, emb2):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Cosine similarity between two embeddings\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    return np.dot(emb1, emb2) / (np.linalg.norm(emb1) * np.linalg.norm(emb2) + 1e-8)\\n\\ndef get_content_words(sentence):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Extract content words (nouns, verbs, adjectives, adverbs) using POS tagging\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    import nltk\\n    from nltk import pos_tag, word_tokenize\\n    try:\\n        tokens = word_tokenize(sentence.lower())\\n        tagged = pos_tag(tokens)\\n        content_pos = {'NN', 'VB', 'JJ', 'RB', 'NNS', 'VBP', 'JJR', 'JJS'}\\n        return set([t[0] for t in tagged if any(t[1].startswith(pos) for pos in content_pos)])\\n    except:\\n        return set()\\n\\ndef lexical_overlap(sent1, sent2):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute lexical overlap ratio of content words\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    words1 = get_content_words(sent1)\\n    words2 = get_content_words(sent2)\\n    if not words1 or not words2:\\n        return 0.0\\n    overlap = len(words1.intersection(words2))\\n    return overlap / max(len(words1), len(words2))\\n\\ndef build_cohesion_network(sentences, embeddings):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Build cohesion network with semantic and lexical edges\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    n = len(sentences)\\n    G = nx.Graph()\\n    G.add_nodes_from(range(n))\\n    \\n    edges = []\\n    for i in range(n):\\n        for j in range(i+1, n):\\n            # Semantic edge: cosine similarity > 0.5\\n            sim = compute_cosine_similarity(embeddings[i], embeddings[j])\\n            semantic_edge = sim > 0.5\\n            \\n            # Lexical edge: content word overlap > 0.3\\n            lex_sim = lexical_overlap(sentences[i], sentences[j])\\n            lexical_edge = lex_sim > 0.3\\n            \\n            if semantic_edge or lexical_edge:\\n                edges.append((i, j, {'semantic': sim, 'lexical': lex_sim}))\\n    \\n    G.add_edges_from(edges)\\n    return G, edges\\n\\n# STEP 4: Percolation Threshold Computation\\ndef compute_percolation_threshold(G, edges, n_iterations=50, alpha=0.5):\\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute percolation threshold via random edge ordering\\\"\\\"\\\"\\n    n_nodes = G.number_of_nodes()\\n    target_size = int(alpha * n_nodes)\\n    thresholds = []\\n    \\n    for _ in range(n_iterations):\\n        # Random edge ordering\\n        shuffled_edges = edges.copy()\\n        np.random.shuffle(shuffled_edges)\\n        \\n        # Add edges incrementally and track giant component\\n        temp_G = nx.Graph()\\n        temp_G.add_nodes_from(range(n_nodes))\\n        \\n        for idx, (u, v, _) in enumerate(shuffled_edges):\\n            temp_G.add_edge(u, v)\\n            # Check largest connected component\\n            components = list(nx.connected_components(temp_G))\\n            largest = max(len(c) for c in components)\\n            \\n            if largest >= target_size:\\n                threshold = idx / len(shuffled_edges)\\n                thresholds.append(threshold)\\n                break\\n        else:\\n            thresholds.append(1.0)  # Never reached threshold\\n    \\n    return np.mean(thresholds), np.std(thresholds)\\n\\n# STEP 5: Main Processing Loop\\nresults = []\\nfor idx, (text_item, (sentences, embeddings)) in enumerate(zip(all_texts, results)):\\n    if sentences is None:\\n        continue  # Skip single-sentence texts\\n    \\n    # Build network\\n    G, edges = build_cohesion_network(sentences, embeddings)\\n    \\n    # Compute percolation threshold\\n    mean_threshold, std_threshold = compute_percolation_threshold(G, edges)\\n    \\n    # Store results\\n    results.append({\\n        'id': idx,\\n        'dataset': text_item['dataset'],\\n        'text': text_item['input'][:200] + '...',  # Truncate for output\\n        'grade_level': text_item['output'],\\n        'percolation_threshold': mean_threshold,\\n        'percolation_std': std_threshold,\\n        'n_sentences': len(sentences),\\n        'n_edges': len(edges)\\n    })\\n    \\n    if idx % 100 == 0:\\n        print(f'Processed {idx}/{len(all_texts)} texts')\\n\\n# STEP 6: Evaluation\\nimport scipy.stats as stats\\n\\n# Convert to arrays\\npercolation_vals = np.array([r['percolation_threshold'] for r in results])\\ngrade_vals = np.array([r['grade_level'] for r in results])\\n\\n# Pearson correlation\\npearson_r, pearson_p = stats.pearsonr(percolation_vals, grade_vals)\\n\\n# Spearman correlation\\nspearman_r, spearman_p = stats.spearmanr(percolation_vals, grade_vals)\\n\\n# R\u00b2 (variance explained)\\nfrom sklearn.linear_model import LinearRegression\\nmodel = LinearRegression()\\nmodel.fit(percolation_vals.reshape(-1, 1), grade_vals)\\nr2 = model.score(percolation_vals.reshape(-1, 1), grade_vals)\\n\\n# RMSE\\nfrom sklearn.metrics import mean_squared_error\\npredictions = model.predict(percolation_vals.reshape(-1, 1))\\nrmse = np.sqrt(mean_squared_error(grade_vals, predictions))\\n\\n# STEP 7: Disaggregated Results by Dataset\\nfor dataset_name in datasets:\\n    subset = [r for r in results if r['dataset'] == dataset_name]\\n    if not subset:\\n        continue\\n    subset_perc = np.array([r['percolation_threshold'] for r in subset])\\n    subset_grade = np.array([r['grade_level'] for r in subset])\\n    \\n    r, p = stats.pearsonr(subset_perc, subset_grade)\\n    print(f'{dataset_name}: r={r:.3f}, p={p:.4f}, compute_flesch_kincaid(text):\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute Flesch-Kincaid Grade Level\\\"\\\"\\\"\n    sentences = [s.strip() for s in re.split(r'[.!?]+', text) if s.strip()]\n    words = text.split()\n    \n    if len(sentences) == 0 or len(words) == 0:\n        return 0.0\n    \n    # Count syllables (approximation)\n    def count_syllables(word):\n        word = word.lower()\n        syllables = 0\n        vowels = 'aeiouy'\n        prev_was_vowel = False\n        for char in word:\n            is_vowel = char in vowels\n            if is_vowel and not prev_was_vowel:\n                syllables += 1\n            prev_was_vowel = is_vowel\n        if word.endswith('e'):\n            syllables -= 1\n        if word.endswith('le') and len(word) > 2 and word[-3] not in vowels:\n            syllables += 1\n        if syllables == 0:\n            syllables = 1\n        return syllables\n    \n    total_syllables = sum(count_syllables(w) for w in words)\n    \n    # Flesch-Kincaid Grade Level\n    asl = len(words) / len(sentences)  # Average Sentence Length\n    asw = total_syllables / len(words)  # Average Syllables per Word\n    fk_grade = 0.39 * asl + 11.8 * asw - 15.59\n    \n    return max(0.0, min(12.0, fk_grade))  # Clamp to [0, 12]\n\n# Add Flesch-Kincaid to all texts\nfor item in all_texts:\n    item['flesch_kincaid'] = compute_flesch_kincaid(item['input'])\n\n# STEP 2: get_sentence_embeddings(text):\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Split text into sentences and compute SBERT embeddings\\\"\\\"\\\"\n    sentences = [s.strip() + '.' for s in text.split('.') if s.strip()]\n    if len(sentences) < 2:\n        return None, None  # Skip single-sentence texts\n    embeddings = model.encode(sentences, show_progress_bar=False)\n    return sentences, embeddings\n\n# Parallel processing for efficiency\nprint(f\"Processing {len(all_texts)} texts with SBERT...\")\nwith Pool(cpu_count()) as pool:\n    embedding_results = pool.map(get_sentence_embeddings, [t['input'] for t in all_texts])\n\n# STEP 3: Cohesion Network Construction\nimport networkx as nx\nimport nltk\nfrom nltk import pos_tag, word_tokenize\n\n# Ensure NLTK data is available\ntry:\n    nltk.data.find('tokenizers/punkt')\nexcept LookupError:\n    nltk.download('punkt')\ntry:\n    nltk.data.find('taggers/averaged_perceptron_tagger')\nexcept LookupError:\n    nltk.download('averaged_perceptron_tagger')\n\ndef compute_cosine_similarity(emb1, emb2):\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Cosine similarity between two embeddings\\\"\\\"\\\"\n    return np.dot(emb1, emb2) / (np.linalg.norm(emb1) * np.linalg.norm(emb2) + 1e-8)\n\ndef get_content_words(sentence):\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Extract content words (nouns, verbs, adjectives, adverbs) using POS tagging\\\"\\\"\\\"\n    try:\n        tokens = word_tokenize(sentence.lower())\n        tagged = pos_tag(tokens)\n        content_pos = {'NN', 'VB', 'JJ', 'RB', 'NNS', 'VBP', 'JJR', 'JJS', 'NNP', 'NNPS'}\n        return set([t[0] for t in tagged if any(t[1].startswith(pos) for pos in content_pos)])\n    except:\n        return set()\n\ndef lexical_overlap(sent1, sent2):\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute lexical overlap ratio of content words\\\"\\\"\\\"\n    words1 = get_content_words(sent1)\n    words2 = get_content_words(sent2)\n    if not words1 or not words2:\n        return 0.0\n    overlap = len(words1.intersection(words2))\n    return overlap / max(len(words1), len(words2))\n\ndef build_cohesion_network(sentences, embeddings, use_semantic=True, use_lexical=True):\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Build cohesion network with semantic and/or lexical edges\\\"\\\"\\\"\n    n = len(sentences)\n    G = nx.Graph()\n    G.add_nodes_from(range(n))\n    \n    edges = []\n    for i in range(n):\n        for j in range(i+1, n):\n            semantic_edge = False\n            lexical_edge = False\n            sim = 0.0\n            lex_sim = 0.0\n            \n            if use_semantic:\n                sim = compute_cosine_similarity(embeddings[i], embeddings[j])\n                semantic_edge = sim > 0.5\n            \n            if use_lexical:\n                lex_sim = lexical_overlap(sentences[i], sentences[j])\n                lexical_edge = lex_sim > 0.3\n            \n            if (use_semantic and semantic_edge) or (use_lexical and lexical_edge):\n                edges.append((i, j, {'semantic': sim, 'lexical': lex_sim}))\n    \n    G.add_edges_from(edges)\n    return G, edges\n\n# STEP 4: Percolation Threshold Computation (optimized with Union-Find)\nclass UnionFind:\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Union-Find data structure for efficient component tracking\\\"\\\"\\\"\n    def __init__(self, n):\n        self.parent = list(range(n))\n        self.size = [1] * n\n        self.max_size = 1\n    \n    def find(self, x):\n        while self.parent[x] != x:\n            self.parent[x] = self.parent[self.parent[x]]\n            x = self.parent[x]\n        return x\n    \n    def union(self, x, y):\n        px, py = self.find(x), self.find(y)\n        if px == py:\n            return\n        if self.size[px] < self.size[py]:\n            px, py = py, px\n        self.parent[py] = px\n        self.size[px] += self.size[py]\n        self.max_size = max(self.max_size, self.size[px])\n\ndef compute_percolation_threshold(n_nodes, edges, n_iterations=50, alpha=0.5):\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute percolation threshold via random edge ordering using Union-Find\\\"\\\"\\\"\n    target_size = int(alpha * n_nodes)\n    thresholds = []\n    \n    for _ in range(n_iterations):\n        # Random edge ordering\n        shuffled_indices = np.random.permutation(len(edges))\n        \n        uf = UnionFind(n_nodes)\n        threshold = 1.0  # Default if never reaches threshold\n        \n        for idx in range(len(shuffled_indices)):\n            edge_idx = shuffled_indices[idx]\n            u, v, _ = edges[edge_idx]\n            uf.union(u, v)\n            \n            if uf.max_size >= target_size:\n                threshold = (idx + 1) / len(edges)\n                break\n        \n        thresholds.append(threshold)\n    \n    return np.mean(thresholds), np.std(thresholds)\n\n# STEP 5: Main Processing Loop\nprint(\"Computing percolation thresholds...\")\nresults = []\n\nfor idx, (text_item, emb_result) in enumerate(zip(all_texts, embedding_results)):\n    sentences, embeddings = emb_result\n    if sentences is None:\n        continue  # Skip single-sentence texts\n    \n    # Build network with both semantic and lexical edges\n    G, edges = build_cohesion_network(sentences, embeddings, use_semantic=True, use_lexical=True)\n    \n    if len(edges) == 0:\n        # No edges found, assign threshold = 1.0 (max difficulty)\n        mean_threshold, std_threshold = 1.0, 0.0\n    else:\n        # Compute percolation threshold\n        mean_threshold, std_threshold = compute_percolation_threshold(len(sentences), edges)\n    \n    # Store results\n    results.append({\n        'id': idx,\n        'dataset': text_item['dataset'],\n        'text': text_item['input'][:200] + '...' if len(text_item['input']) > 200 else text_item['input'],\n        'grade_level': text_item['output'],\n        'flesch_kincaid': text_item['flesch_kincaid'],\n        'percolation_threshold': float(mean_threshold),\n        'percolation_std': float(std_threshold),\n        'n_sentences': len(sentences),\n        'n_edges': len(edges)\n    })\n    \n    if (idx + 1) % 100 == 0:\n        print(f'Processed {idx + 1}/{len(all_texts)} texts')\n\nprint(f\"Completed processing {len(results)} texts\")\n\n# STEP 6: Evaluation Metrics\nimport scipy.stats as stats\nfrom sklearn.linear_model import LinearRegression\nfrom sklearn.metrics import mean_squared_error\n\n# Convert to arrays\npercolation_vals = np.array([r['percolation_threshold'] for r in results])\ngrade_vals = np.array([r['grade_level'] for r in results])\nfk_vals = np.array([r['flesch_kincaid'] for r in results])\n\n# Primary correlation: percolation threshold vs grade level (should be POSITIVE)\npearson_r, pearson_p = stats.pearsonr(percolation_vals, grade_vals)\nspearman_r, spearman_p = stats.spearmanr(percolation_vals, grade_vals)\n\nprint(f\"\\\\n=== MAIN RESULTS ===\")\nprint(f\"Percolation vs Grade Level: r={pearson_r:.4f}, p={pearson_p:.6f}\")\n\n# R\u00b2 and RMSE\nlr_model = LinearRegression()\nlr_model.fit(percolation_vals.reshape(-1, 1), grade_vals)\nr2 = lr_model.score(percolation_vals.reshape(-1, 1), grade_vals)\npredictions = lr_model.predict(percolation_vals.reshape(-1, 1))\nrmse = np.sqrt(mean_squared_error(grade_vals, predictions))\n\nprint(f\"R\u00b2 = {r2:.4f}\")\nprint(f\"RMSE = {rmse:.4f} grade levels\")\n\n# Traditional metrics baseline (Flesch-Kincaid)\nfk_pearson_r, fk_pearson_p = stats.pearsonr(fk_vals, grade_vals)\nfk_lr = LinearRegression()\nfk_lr.fit(fk_vals.reshape(-1, 1), grade_vals)\nfk_r2 = fk_lr.score(fk_vals.reshape(-1, 1), grade_vals)\n\nprint(f\"\\\\n=== BASELINE COMPARISON ===\")\nprint(f\"Flesch-Kincaid vs Grade Level: r={fk_pearson_r:.4f}, R\u00b2={fk_r2:.4f}\")\n\n# Combined model (percolation + Flesch-Kincaid)\nfrom sklearn.linear_model import Ridge\nX_combined = np.column_stack([percolation_vals, fk_vals])\ncombined_model = Ridge()\ncombined_model.fit(X_combined, grade_vals)\ncombined_r2 = combined_model.score(X_combined, grade_vals)\nprint(f\"Combined model compute_flesch_kincaid(text):\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute Flesch-Kincaid Grade Level\\\"\\\"\\\"\n    sentences = [s.strip() for s in re.split(r'[.!?]+', text) if s.strip()]\n    words = text.split()\n    \n    if len(sentences) == 0 or len(words) == 0:\n        return 0.0\n    \n    # Count syllables (approximation)\n    def count_syllables(word):\n        word = word.lower()\n        syllables = 0\n        vowels = 'aeiouy'\n        prev_was_vowel = False\n        for char in word:\n            is_vowel = char in vowels\n            if is_vowel and not prev_was_vowel:\n                syllables += 1\n            prev_was_vowel = is_vowel\n        if word.endswith('e'):\n            syllables -= 1\n        if word.endswith('le') and len(word) > 2 and word[-3] not in vowels:\n            syllables += 1\n        if syllables == 0:\n            syllables = 1\n        return syllables\n    \n    total_syllables = sum(count_syllables(w) for w in words)\n    \n    # Flesch-Kincaid Grade Level\n    asl = len(words) / len(sentences)  # Average Sentence Length\n    asw = total_syllables / len(words)  # Average Syllables per Word\n    fk_grade = 0.39 * asl + 11.8 * asw - 15.59\n    \n    return max(0.0, min(12.0, fk_grade))  # Clamp to [0, 12]\n\n# Add Flesch-Kincaid to all texts\nfor item in all_texts:\n    item['flesch_kincaid'] = compute_flesch_kincaid(item['input'])\n\n# STEP 2: SBERT Embedding Computation\nfrom sentence_transformers import SentenceTransformer\n\nprint(\"Loading SBERT model...\")\nmodel = SentenceTransformer('all-MiniLM-L6-v2')\n\ndef get_sentence_embeddings(text):\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Split text into sentences and compute SBERT embeddings\\\"\\\"\\\"\n    sentences = [s.strip() + '.' for s in text.split('.') if s.strip()]\n    if len(sentences) < 2:\n        return None, None  # Skip single-sentence texts\n    embeddings = model.encode(sentences, show_progress_bar=False)\n    return sentences, embeddings\n\n# Parallel processing for efficiency\nprint(f\"Processing {len(all_texts)} texts with SBERT...\")\nwith Pool(cpu_count()) as pool:\n    embedding_results = pool.map(get_sentence_embeddings, [t['input'] for t in all_texts])\n\n# STEP 3: Cohesion Network Construction\nimport networkx as nx\nimport nltk\nfrom nltk import pos_tag, word_tokenize\n\n# Ensure NLTK data is available\ntry:\n    nltk.data.find('tokenizers/punkt')\nexcept LookupError:\n    nltk.download('punkt')\ntry:\n    nltk.data.find('taggers/averaged_perceptron_tagger')\nexcept LookupError:\n    nltk.download('averaged_perceptron_tagger')\n\ndef compute_cosine_similarity(emb1, emb2):\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Cosine similarity between two embeddings\\\"\\\"\\\"\n    return np.dot(emb1, emb2) / (np.linalg.norm(emb1) * np.linalg.norm(emb2) + 1e-8)\n\ndef get_content_words(sentence):\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Extract content words (nouns, verbs, adjectives, adverbs) using POS tagging\\\"\\\"\\\"\n    try:\n        tokens = word_tokenize(sentence.lower())\n        tagged = pos_tag(tokens)\n        content_pos = {'NN', 'VB', 'JJ', 'RB', 'NNS', 'VBP', 'JJR', 'JJS', 'NNP', 'NNPS'}\n        return set([t[0] for t in tagged if any(t[1].startswith(pos) for pos in content_pos)])\n    except:\n        return set()\n\ndef lexical_overlap(sent1, sent2):\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute lexical overlap ratio of content words\\\"\\\"\\\"\n    words1 = get_content_words(sent1)\n    words2 = get_content_words(sent2)\n    if not words1 or not words2:\n        return 0.0\n    overlap = len(words1.intersection(words2))\n    return overlap / max(len(words1), len(words2))\n\ndef build_cohesion_network(sentences, embeddings, use_semantic=True, use_lexical=True):\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Build cohesion network with semantic and/or lexical edges\\\"\\\"\\\"\n    n = len(sentences)\n    G = nx.Graph()\n    G.add_nodes_from(range(n))\n    \n    edges = []\n    for i in range(n):\n        for j in range(i+1, n):\n            semantic_edge = False\n            lexical_edge = False\n            sim = 0.0\n            lex_sim = 0.0\n            \n            if use_semantic:\n                sim = compute_cosine_similarity(embeddings[i], embeddings[j])\n                semantic_edge = sim > 0.5\n            \n            if use_lexical:\n                lex_sim = lexical_overlap(sentences[i], sentences[j])\n                lexical_edge = lex_sim > 0.3\n            \n            if (use_semantic and semantic_edge) or (use_lexical and lexical_edge):\n                edges.append((i, j, {'semantic': sim, 'lexical': lex_sim}))\n    \n    G.add_edges_from(edges)\n    return G, edges\n\n# STEP 4: Percolation Threshold Computation (optimized with Union-Find)\nclass UnionFind:\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Union-Find data structure for efficient component tracking\\\"\\\"\\\"\n    def __init__(self, n):\n        self.parent = list(range(n))\n        self.size = [1] * n\n        self.max_size = 1\n    \n    def find(self, x):\n        while self.parent[x] != x:\n            self.parent[x] = self.parent[self.parent[x]]\n            x = self.parent[x]\n        return x\n    \n    def union(self, x, y):\n        px, py = self.find(x), self.find(y)\n        if px == py:\n            return\n        if self.size[px] < self.size[py]:\n            px, py = py, px\n        self.parent[py] = px\n        self.size[px] += self.size[py]\n        self.max_size = max(self.max_size, self.size[px])\n\ndef compute_percolation_threshold(n_nodes, edges, n_iterations=50, alpha=0.5):\n    \\\"\\\"\\\"Compute percolation threshold via random edge ordering using Union-Find\\\"\\\"\\\"\n    target_size = int(alpha * n_nodes)\n    thresholds = []\n    \n    for _ in range(n_iterations):\n        # Random edge ordering\n        shuffled_indices = np.random.permutation(len(edges))\n        \n        uf = UnionFind(n_nodes)\n        threshold = 1.0  # Default if never reaches threshold\n        \n        for idx in range(len(shuffled_indices)):\n            edge_idx = shuffled_indices[idx]\n            u, v, _ = edges[edge_idx]\n            uf.union(u, v)\n            \n            if uf.max_size >= target_size:\n                threshold = (idx + 1) / len(edges)\n                break\n        \n        thresholds.append(threshold)\n    \n    return np.mean(thresholds), np.std(thresholds)\n\n# STEP 5: Main Processing Loop\nprint(\"Computing percolation thresholds...\")\nresults = []\n\nfor idx, (text_item, emb_result) in enumerate(zip(all_texts, embedding_results)):\n    sentences, embeddings = emb_result\n    if sentences is None:\n        continue  # Skip single-sentence texts\n    \n    # Build network with both semantic and lexical edges\n    G, edges = build_cohesion_network(sentences, embeddings, use_semantic=True, use_lexical=True)\n    \n    if len(edges) == 0:\n        # No edges found, assign threshold = 1.0 (max difficulty)\n        mean_threshold, std_threshold = 1.0, 0.0\n    else:\n        # Compute percolation threshold\n        mean_threshold, std_threshold = compute_percolation_threshold(len(sentences), edges)\n    \n    # Store results\n    results.append({\n        'id': idx,\n        'dataset': text_item['dataset'],\n        'text': text_item['input'][:200] + '...' if len(text_item['input']) > 200 else text_item['input'],\n        'grade_level': text_item['output'],\n        'flesch_kincaid': text_item['flesch_kincaid'],\n        'percolation_threshold': float(mean_threshold),\n        'percolation_std': float(std_threshold),\n        'n_sentences': len(sentences),\n        'n_edges': len(edges)\n    })\n    \n    if (idx + 1) % 100 == 0:\n        print(f'Processed {idx + 1}/{len(all_texts)} texts')\n\nprint(f\"Completed processing {len(results)} texts\")\n\n# STEP 6: Evaluation Metrics\nimport scipy.stats as stats\nfrom sklearn.linear_model import LinearRegression\nfrom sklearn.metrics import mean_squared_error\n\n# Convert to arrays\npercolation_vals = np.array([r['percolation_threshold'] for r in results])\ngrade_vals = np.array([r['grade_level'] for r in results])\nfk_vals = np.array([r['flesch_kincaid'] for r in results])\n\n# Primary correlation: percolation threshold vs grade level (should be POSITIVE)\npearson_r, pearson_p = stats.pearsonr(percolation_vals, grade_vals)\nspearman_r, spearman_p = stats.spearmanr(percolation_vals, grade_vals)\n\nprint(f\"\\\\n=== MAIN RESULTS ===\")\nprint(f\"Percolation vs Grade Level: r={pearson_r:.4f}, p={pearson_p:.6f}\")\n\n# R\u00b2 and RMSE\nlr_model = LinearRegression()\nlr_model.fit(percolation_vals.reshape(-1, 1), grade_vals)\nr2 = lr_model.score(percolation_vals.reshape(-1, 1), grade_vals)\npredictions = lr_model.predict(percolation_vals.reshape(-1, 1))\nrmse = np.sqrt(mean_squared_error(grade_vals, predictions))\n\nprint(f\"R\u00b2 = {r2:.4f}\")\nprint(f\"RMSE = {rmse:.4f} grade levels\")\n\n# Traditional metrics baseline (Flesch-Kincaid)\nfk_pearson_r, fk_pearson_p = stats.pearsonr(fk_vals, grade_vals)\nfk_lr = LinearRegression()\nfk_lr.fit(fk_vals.reshape(-1, 1), grade_vals)\nfk_r2 = fk_lr.score(fk_vals.reshape(-1, 1), grade_vals)\n\nprint(f\"\\\\n=== BASELINE COMPARISON ===\")\nprint(f\"Flesch-Kincaid vs Grade Level: r={fk_pearson_r:.4f}, R\u00b2={fk_r2:.4f}\")\n\n# Combined model (percolation + Flesch-Kincaid)\nfrom sklearn.linear_model import Ridge\nX_combined = np.column_stack([percolation_vals, fk_vals])\ncombined_model = Ridge()\ncombined_model.fit(X_combined, grade_vals)\ncombined_r2 = combined_model.score(X_combined, grade_vals)\nprint(f\"Combined model R\u00b2 = {combined_r2:.4f} (\u0394R\u00b2 = {combined_r2 - max(r2, fk_r2):.4f})\")\n\n# STEP 7: Disaggregated Results by Dataset\nprint(f\"\\\\n=== DISAGGREGATED RESULTS ===\")\ndisaggregated =
